<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Long-term fundamentals and strategy remain intact; full-year 2020 outlook withdrawn due to uncertainty around the
impact of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19</FONT> on financial and operating results </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">CHICAGO, Ill. &#150;
April&nbsp;28, 2020 &#150; Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (NASDAQ: MDLZ) today reported its first quarter 2020 results. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;We had a
strong first quarter, with record market share gains and executed very well in challenging circumstances, thanks to the dedication and commitment of our colleagues, especially those on the front line, who are working tirelessly to provide food to
consumers around the world,&#148; said Dirk Van de Put, Chairman and Chief Executive Officer. &#147;In the last month of the quarter, we saw a significant increase in consumer demand for our snacks in developed markets, particularly in North
America, which more than offset a more challenging environment in several emerging markets. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;Our priority at this time is to protect
our colleagues and maintain business continuity in service of our customers and consumers around the world. We remain confident that with our dedicated people, our portfolio of trusted global and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">taste-of-the-nation</FONT></FONT></FONT> local brands, our strong balance sheet, access to significant liquidity and our clear strategic priorities, we have everything we need to manage
through this pandemic and emerge stronger on the other side.&#148; </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><U>Our priorities are clear in a volatile, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19</FONT> environment
</U></I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During this global crisis, our priorities are clear and informed by our values. Our first priority is to protect and support the
safety and well-being of our employees. We have introduced strict health and safety protocols across our facilities and are providing enhanced benefits for front-line employees. We are supporting community partners advancing critical food stability
and emergency relief efforts across the world with both cash donations and products. We have donated $20&nbsp;million to date. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">After
colleagues and communities, our next priority is supply chain continuity, so we are focusing on the most important products for retailers and consumers to maintain good service levels. Through this uncertain time, we are exercising cost discipline
and protecting cash by reducing <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-critical</FONT> spending. We have expanded our credit facilities and suspended our share repurchase program at this time. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We are intent on emerging from this crisis even stronger than before. We are accelerating a number of strategic initiatives and continuing to
invest in our brands and capabilities to remain the preferred choice of our customers and consumers. </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><U>First Quarter Commentary </U></I></P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Net revenues</B> increased 2.6&nbsp;percent driven by Organic Net Revenue growth of 6.4% offset by unfavorable
currency impacts. As a result of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19,</FONT> growth rates accelerated in developed markets and slowed in emerging markets versus Q4 2019. Volume/mix was the largest driver of growth, while pricing contributed to
growth at approximately the same level as the prior quarter. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Gross profit </B>decreased $142&nbsp;million and margin declined 320 basis points to 36.5&nbsp;percent, due to
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> losses from derivatives. Adjusted Gross Profit<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP> increased $151&nbsp;million at constant currency
while Adjusted Growth Profit margin decreased 20 basis points to 39.6&nbsp;percent primarily due to higher raw material costs in part due to unfavorable currency movements, and disruption caused by <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19.</FONT>
</P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Operating income </B>decreased $180&nbsp;million and margin was 12.8&nbsp;percent, down 300 basis points
primarily due to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> losses from currency and commodities derivatives. Adjusted Operating Income<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP>
increased $62&nbsp;million at constant currency, and margin decreased 30 basis points to 16.5&nbsp;percent driven primarily by the decline in Adjusted Gross Profit margin and higher marketing expenses, partially offset by pricing and overhead costs
leverage. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Diluted EPS</B> was $0.52, down 17.5%, primarily due to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> losses from derivatives and losses related to interest rate swaps. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Adjusted EPS</B> was $0.69, up 10.8% versus prior year on a constant-currency basis driven by operating gains
as well as higher JV income, share repurchases, lower taxes and higher benefit plan <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-service</FONT> income. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Capital Return</B>: The company returned approximately $1.1&nbsp;billion to shareholders in common stock
repurchases and cash dividends. The company suspended its share repurchase program in March, providing flexibility and prioritizing cash and liquidity while managing the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19</FONT> situation and response.
</P></TD></TR></TABLE>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>2020 Outlook </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Due to the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19</FONT> pandemic, visibility is limited at this time in a number of markets, so the company
is temporarily withdrawing its full-year outlook. The company strategy and long-term algorithm remain unchanged. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Conference Call </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International will host a conference call for investors with accompanying slides to review its results at 5 p.m. ET today. A
listen-only webcast will be provided at <U>www.mondelezinternational.com</U>. An archive of the webcast will be available on the company&#146;s web site. The company will be live tweeting the event at <U>www.twitter.com/MDLZ</U>. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>About Mondel&#275;z International </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (NASDAQ: MDLZ) empowers people to snack right in over 150 countries around the world. With 2019 net revenues
of approximately $26&nbsp;billion, MDLZ is leading the future of snacking with iconic global and local brands such as <I>Oreo</I>, <I>belVita</I> and <I>LU</I> biscuits; <I>Cadbury Dairy Milk</I>, <I>Milka</I> and <I>Toblerone</I> chocolate; <I>Sour
Patch Kids</I> candy and <I>Trident</I> gum. Mondel&#275;z International is a proud member of the Standard and Poor&#146;s 500, Nasdaq 100 and Dow Jones Sustainability Index. Visit <U>www.mondelezinternational.com</U> or follow the company on
Twitter at <U>www.twitter.com/MDLZ</U>. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>End Notes </B></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="4%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">1.</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">Organic Net Revenue, Adjusted Gross Profit (and Adjusted Gross Profit margin), Adjusted Operating Income (and
Adjusted Operating Income margin), Adjusted EPS, Free Cash Flow and presentation of amounts in constant currency are <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures. Please see discussion of
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures at the end of this press release for more information. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>

<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Additional Definitions </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Emerging markets
consist of the Latin America region in its entirety; the Asia, Middle East and Africa region excluding Australia, New Zealand and Japan; and the following countries from the Europe region: Russia, Ukraine, Turkey, Kazakhstan, Georgia, Poland, Czech
Republic, Slovak Republic, Hungary, Bulgaria, Romania, the Baltics and the East Adriatic countries. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Developed markets include the entire
North America region, the Europe region excluding the countries included in the emerging markets definition, and Australia, New Zealand and Japan from the Asia, Middle East and Africa region. </P>

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. and Subsidiaries </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Reconciliation of GAAP and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Financial Measures </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>(Unaudited) </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company reports its
financial results in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States (&#147;GAAP&#148;). However, management believes that also presenting certain <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures
provides additional information to facilitate the comparison of the company&#146;s historical operating results and trends in its underlying operating results, and provides additional transparency on how the company evaluates its business.
Management uses these <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures in making financial, operating and planning decisions and in evaluating the company&#146;s performance. The company also believes that presenting these
measures allows investors to view its performance using the same measures that the company uses in evaluating its financial and business performance and trends. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company considers quantitative and qualitative factors in assessing whether to adjust for the impact of items that may be significant or that could affect
an understanding of its ongoing financial and business performance and trends. The adjustments generally fall within the following categories: acquisition&nbsp;&amp; divestiture activities, gains and losses on intangible asset sales and <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> impairments, major program restructuring activities, constant currency and related adjustments, major program financing and hedging activities and other major items affecting comparability of operating
results. See below for a description of adjustments to the company&#146;s U.S. GAAP financial measures included herein. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> information should be considered as supplemental in nature and is not meant to be considered in isolation or
as a substitute for the related financial information prepared in accordance with U.S. GAAP. In addition, the company&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures may not be the same as or comparable to similar <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures presented by other companies. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>DEFINITIONS OF THE COMPANY&#146;S
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">NON-GAAP</FONT> FINANCIAL MEASURES </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial
measures and corresponding metrics reflect how the company evaluates its operating results currently and provide improved comparability of operating results. As new events or circumstances arise, these definitions could change. When these
definitions change, the company provides the updated definitions and presents the related <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> historical results on a comparable basis. When items no longer impact the company&#146;s current or future
presentation of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> operating results, the company removes these items from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> definitions. </P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Organic Net Revenue&#148;</B> is defined as net revenues excluding the impacts of acquisitions,
divestitures and currency rate fluctuations. The company also evaluates Organic Net Revenue growth from emerging markets and developed markets. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Adjusted Gross Profit&#148;</B> is defined as gross profit excluding the impacts of the Simplify to Grow
Program; acquisition integration costs; the operating results of divestitures; <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivative
contracts; and incremental expenses related to the 2017 malware incident. The company also presents &#147;Adjusted Gross Profit margin,&#148; which is subject to the same adjustments as Adjusted Gross Profit. The company also evaluates growth in the
company&#146;s Adjusted Gross Profit on a constant currency basis. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Adjusted Operating Income&#148;</B> and <B>&#147;Adjusted Segment Operating Income&#148;</B> are defined
as operating income (or segment operating income) excluding the impacts of the items listed in the Adjusted Gross Profit definition as well as gains or losses (including <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> impairment charges) on
goodwill and intangible assets; divestiture or acquisition gains or losses and related divestiture, acquisition and integration costs; remeasurement of net monetary position; impacts from resolution of tax matters; CEO transition remuneration; Swiss
tax reform impacts; and impact from pension participation changes. The company also presents &#147;Adjusted Operating Income margin&#148; and &#147;Adjusted Segment Operating Income margin,&#148; which are subject to the same adjustments as Adjusted
Operating Income and Adjusted Segment Operating Income. The company also evaluates growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted Operating Income and Adjusted Segment Operating Income on a constant currency basis. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

continuing operations excluding the impacts of the items listed in the Adjusted Operating Income definition, as well as losses on debt extinguishment and related expenses; gains or losses on equity method investment transactions; net earnings from
divestitures; gains or losses on interest rate swaps no longer designated as accounting cash flow hedges due to changed financing and hedging plans; and U.S. and Swiss tax reform impacts. Similarly, within Adjusted EPS, the company&#146;s equity
method investment net earnings exclude its proportionate share of its investees&#146; unusual or infrequent items. The tax impact of each of the items excluded from the company&#146;s GAAP results was computed based on the facts and tax assumptions
associated with each item, and such impacts have also been excluded from Adjusted EPS. The company also evaluates growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted EPS on a constant currency basis. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>

expenditures. Free Cash Flow is the company&#146;s primary measure used to monitor its cash flow performance. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">See the attached

<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>SEGMENT OPERATING INCOME </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company uses segment operating income to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. The company believes it is appropriate to disclose this
measure to help investors analyze segment performance and trends. Segment operating income excludes unrealized gains and losses on hedging activities (which are a component of cost of sales), general corporate expenses (which are a component of
selling, general and administrative expenses), amortization of intangibles, gains and losses on divestitures and acquisition-related costs (which are a component of selling, general and administrative expenses) in all periods presented. The company
excludes these items from segment operating income in order to provide better transparency of its segment operating results. Furthermore, the company centrally manages benefit plan <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-service</FONT> income and
interest and other expense, net. Accordingly, the company does not present these items by segment because they are excluded from the segment profitability measure that management reviews. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>ITEMS IMPACTING COMPARABILITY OF OPERATING RESULTS </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The
following information is provided to give qualitative and quantitative information related to items impacting comparability of operating results. The company identifies these based on how management views the company&#146;s business; makes
financial, operating and planning decisions; and evaluates the company&#146;s ongoing performance. In addition, the company discloses the impact of changes in currency exchange rates on the company&#146;s financial results in order to reflect
results on a constant currency basis. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Divestitures, Divestiture-related costs and Gains/(losses) on Divestitures </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Divestitures include completed sales of businesses and exits of major product lines upon completion of a sale or licensing agreement. </P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">On May&nbsp;28, 2019, the company completed the sale of most of its cheese business in the Middle East and Africa
to Arla Foods of Denmark and recorded a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $44&nbsp;million on the sale. During the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2019, the company reversed $1&nbsp;million of divestiture-related expenses
accrued in the fourth quarter of 2018 that were no longer required. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Acquisitions, Acquisition-related costs and Acquisition
integration costs </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On April&nbsp;1, 2020, the company acquired a significant majority interest in Give&nbsp;&amp; Go, a North American leader in
fully-finished sweet baked goods and owners of the famous <I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">two-bite</FONT></I><I><SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">&reg;</SUP></I> brand of brownies and the <I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Create-A-Treat</FONT></FONT></I><I><SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">&reg;</SUP></I> brand, known for cookie and gingerbread house decorating kits. During the first quarter of 2020, the company incurred
$5&nbsp;million of acquisition-related costs. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On July&nbsp;16, 2019, the company acquired a majority interest in a U.S. refrigerated nutrition bar
company, Perfect Snacks, within its North America segment. The acquisition added incremental net revenues of $32&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On June&nbsp;7, 2018, the company acquired a U.S. premium biscuit company, Tate&#146;s Bake Shop, within its North America segment and extended its premium
biscuit offerings. The company incurred acquisition-integration costs of $1&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Simplify to
Grow Program </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The primary objective of the Simplify to Grow Program is to reduce the company&#146;s operating cost structure in both its supply
chain and overhead costs. The program covers severance as well as asset disposals and other manufacturing and procurement-related <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-time</FONT> costs. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Restructuring costs </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company recorded restructuring
charges of $15&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020 and $20&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2019 within asset impairment and exit costs and benefit plan <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-service</FONT>
income. These charges were for <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> asset write-downs (including accelerated depreciation and asset impairments), severance and other related costs. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Implementation costs </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Implementation costs primarily
relate to reorganizing the company&#146;s operations and facilities in connection with its supply chain reinvention program and other identified productivity and cost saving initiatives. The costs include incremental expenses related to the closure
of facilities, costs to terminate certain contracts and the simplification of the company&#146;s information systems. The company recorded implementation costs of $43&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020 and $50&nbsp;million in
the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2019. </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts
from commodity and currency derivative contracts </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company excludes unrealized gains and losses <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts) from outstanding commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> earnings measures until such time that the related
exposures impact its operating results. The company recorded net unrealized losses on commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives of $184&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020 and recorded net unrealized gains of
$16&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2019. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Remeasurement of net monetary position </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the second quarter of 2018, primarily based on published estimates which indicated that Argentina&#146;s three-year cumulative inflation rate exceeded
100%, the company concluded that Argentina became a highly inflationary economy for accounting purposes. As of July&nbsp;1, 2018, the company began to apply highly inflationary accounting for its Argentinian subsidiaries and changed their functional
currency from the Argentinian peso to the U.S. dollar. On July&nbsp;1, 2018, both monetary and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-monetary</FONT> assets and liabilities denominated in Argentinian pesos were remeasured into U.S. dollars. As of each
subsequent balance sheet date, Argentinian peso denominated monetary assets and liabilities were remeasured into U.S. dollars using the exchange rate as of the balance sheet date, with remeasurement and other transaction gains and losses recorded in
net earnings. Within selling, general and administrative expenses, the company recorded a remeasurement loss of $2&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020, as well as a remeasurement loss of $2&nbsp;million in the three months
ended March&nbsp;31, 2019 related to the revaluation of the Argentinian peso denominated net monetary position over these periods. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Impact from
pension participation changes </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The impact from pension participation changes represent the charges incurred when employee groups are withdrawn from
multiemployer pension plans and other changes in employee group pension plan participation. The company excludes these charges from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> results because those amounts do not reflect the company&#146;s
ongoing pension obligations. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On July&nbsp;11, 2019, the company received an undiscounted withdrawal liability assessment from the Fund totaling
$526&nbsp;million and requiring <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pro-rata</FONT> monthly payments over 20 years. The company began making monthly payments during the third quarter of 2019. The company recorded $3&nbsp;million of accreted interest in
the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020. As of March&nbsp;31, 2020, the remaining discounted withdrawal liability was $387&nbsp;million, with $14&nbsp;million recorded in other current liabilities and $373&nbsp;million recorded in long-term other
liabilities. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>CEO transition remuneration </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On
November&nbsp;20, 2017, Dirk Van de Put succeeded Irene Rosenfeld as CEO of Mondel&#275;z International. In order to incent Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put to join the company, the company provided him compensation to make him whole for incentive awards he
forfeited or grants that were not made to him when he left his former employer. In connection with Irene Rosenfeld&#146;s retirement, the company made her outstanding grants of performance share units for the 2016-2018 and 2017-2019 performance
cycles eligible for continued vesting and paid $0.5&nbsp;million salary for her service as Chairman from January through March 2018. The company refers to these elements of Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put&#146;s and Ms.&nbsp;Rosenfeld&#146;s compensation
arrangements together as &#147;CEO transition remuneration.&#148; </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company is excluding amounts it expenses as CEO transition remuneration from its <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> results because those amounts are not part of the company&#146;s regular compensation program and are incremental to amounts the company would have incurred as ongoing CEO compensation. As a result, in
2017, the company excluded amounts expensed for the cash payment to Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put and partial vesting of his equity grants. In 2018, the company excluded amounts paid for Ms.&nbsp;Rosenfeld&#146;s service as Chairman and partial vesting of
Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put&#146;s and Ms.&nbsp;Rosenfeld&#146;s equity grants. In 2019, the company excluded amounts related to the partial vesting of Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put&#146;s equity grants. During the first quarter of 2020, Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put&#146;s
equity grants became fully vested. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Gains/losses related to interest rate swaps </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Within interest and other expense, net, the company recognized an <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax</FONT> loss of $79&nbsp;million ($103&nbsp;million
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax)</FONT> in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020, related to certain forward-starting interest rate swaps for which the planned timing and currency of the related forecasted debt was changed. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Gains and losses on equity method investment transactions </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On July&nbsp;9, 2018, Keurig Green Mountain, Inc. (&#147;Keurig&#148;) closed on its definitive merger agreement with Dr Pepper Snapple Group, Inc., and formed
Keurig Dr Pepper Inc. (NYSE: &#147;KDP&#148;), a publicly traded company. Following the close of the transaction, the company&#146;s 24.2% investment in Keurig together with its shareholder loan receivable became a 13.8% investment in KDP. During
2018, the company recorded a net <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $778&nbsp;million (or $586&nbsp;million <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax</FONT> gain). </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In connection with this transaction, the company changed its accounting principle during the third quarter
of 2018 to reflect its share of Keurig&#146;s historical and KDP&#146;s ongoing earnings on a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-quarter</FONT> lag basis while the company continues to record dividends when cash is received. The company determined
a lag was preferable as it enables the company to continue to report its quarterly and annual results on a timely basis and to record its share of KDP&#146;s ongoing results once KDP has publicly reported its results. The change was retrospectively
applied to all prior periods presented. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the first quarter of 2019, the company recognized a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain
of $23&nbsp;million (or $18&nbsp;million <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax)</FONT> related to the impact of a KDP acquisition that decreased the company&#146;s ownership interest from 13.8% to 13.6%. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On March&nbsp;4, 2020, the company participated in a secondary offering of KDP shares and sold approximately 6.8&nbsp;million shares, which reduced its
ownership interest by 0.5% to 13.1% of the total outstanding shares. The company received $185&nbsp;million of proceeds and recorded a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $71&nbsp;million (or $54&nbsp;million <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax)</FONT> during the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Equity method investee acquisition-related or other
charges/benefits, net </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Within Adjusted EPS, the company&#146;s equity method investment net earnings exclude its proportionate share of its equity
method investees&#146; unusual or infrequent items, such as acquisition and divestiture-related costs, restructuring program costs and discrete U.S. tax reform impacts. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Constant currency </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Management evaluates the
operating performance of the company and its international subsidiaries on a constant currency basis. The company determines its constant currency operating results by dividing or multiplying, as appropriate, the current period local currency
operating results by the currency exchange rates used to translate the company&#146;s financial statements in the comparable prior-year period to determine what the current-period U.S. dollar operating results would have been if the currency
exchange rate had not changed from the comparable prior-year period. </P>
</DIV></Center>
